<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1027223210669908028 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1027223210669908028><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/113136451457146880/0275ef289c9e7b6338d7b72e8f4f2fca.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=i_._i data-user-id=113136451457146880>dean</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, October 5, 2022 11:18 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1027223210669908028>10/5/2022 11:18 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>But SQL doesn&#39;t allow trailing commas. In python, this is OK: 
<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline language-python">l = [thing_a, thing_b, thing_c,]</code>
In SQL, this is a syntax error: 
<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline language-sql">select col_a, col_b, col_c,
from ...</code></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Wednesday, October 5, 2022 11:18 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1032898016656498778 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1032898016656498778><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/426322222324645890/0556cab10701e904711a9a0e6c94a3d9.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/265514283901779970/257922a3b0fe6c0d1c40e94b7e10a655.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=corvuscrypto>Birdy (SE)</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1032894713109426258')"> Is the cayman still listed on the AML blacklist in Europe? Keep in mind if this is the case some folks would get permanent marks on their bank record if they ever transferred money from cayman to Europe (or vice versa) if so and that should be made clear </span> <span class=chatlog__reply-edited-timestamp title="Friday, October 21, 2022 2:57 AM">(edited)</span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=mariaannk data-user-id=426322222324645890>Maria / WaveClef</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, October 21, 2022 3:07 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1032898016656498778>10/21/2022 3:07 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Investment Funds and EU Marketing

Inclusion on the EU AML List shall not prevent Cayman Islands investment funds from being marketed into the EU under national private placement rules under the Alternative Investment Fund Managers Directive (EU) 2011/61 (&quot;AIFMD&quot;).  However, in November 2021 the European Commission published proposals to amend AIFMD.  If the Cayman Islands is added to the EU AML List and remains on it at the point that the proposed AIFMD changes come into effect, this could theoretically restrict Cayman Islands domiciled investment funds from marketing in the EU under the national private placement regimes.  However, the AIFMD proposals are not expected to take effect until 2024 and may be impacted by planned EU AML law changes in the interim, as discussed below.

EU Public Funding

EU-related development agencies may not be able to lend development funding to the Cayman Islands or to entities established in the Cayman Islands, subject to certain exceptions.  However, we understand that this facility is not broadly used in practice and, therefore, we would not expect this to have a material impact.

Tax Implications

Inclusion on the EU AML List should not impact any existing representations or commitments made by tax authorities under agreements with the Cayman Islands in the area of international mutual tax cooperation.  Equally, the listing is not a tax measure so would not, for example, have any impact on dealings with Cayman Islands counterparties under the EU&#39;s DAC6 tax reporting regime.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1032898147279708312 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1032898147279708312><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Friday, October 21, 2022 3:08 AM">3:08 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><a href="https://maples.com/en/knowledge-centre/2022/1/cayman-islands-and-the-eu-aml-high-risk-third-countries-list">https://maples.com/en/knowledge-centre/2022/1/cayman-islands-and-the-eu-aml-high-risk-third-countries-list</a></span></div><div class=chatlog__embed><div class="chatlog__embed-color-pill chatlog__embed-color-pill--default"></div><div class=chatlog__embed-content-container><div class=chatlog__embed-content><div class=chatlog__embed-text><div class=chatlog__embed-title><a class=chatlog__embed-title-link href=https://maples.com/en/knowledge-centre/2022/1/cayman-islands-and-the-eu-aml-high-risk-third-countries-list><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">Cayman Islands and the EU AML High-Risk Third Countries List</div></a></div><div class=chatlog__embed-description><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">This update briefly analyses the practical consequences of the Cayman Islands&#39; potential addition to the EU AML List for clients using Cayman Islands vehicles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div>

id=chatlog__message-container-1034063013197664257 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1034063013197664257><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, October 24, 2022 8:17 AM">8:17 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>say from scratch you run a query to do a group by on a table with 14GB of data, it will read the pages into memory (claiming 14GB) and then claim some more for the hash table (say 1GB)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1034063188389535824 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1034063188389535824><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, October 24, 2022 8:17 AM">8:17 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>when the query is finished, you have 15GB of memory reserved, 14GB of which is data pages and 1GB is empty because the hash table is ephemeral</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1034063309726548020 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1034063309726548020><div <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1035790453133545482 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1035790453133545482><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rakkit. data-user-id=209245848960368641>rakkit.</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, October 29, 2022 2:41 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1035790453133545482>10/29/2022 2:41 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><span class="chatlog__markdown-mention" title="trs800373">@TRS-80</span> we do, the problem isn&#39;t currently blocking though.
The issue is that I get re-reads of rows from tables that loaded during the dataset being produced.
We batch pull from prod every 5mins/hourly due to the size of the data to make it manageable, and we need &quot;live reports&quot; (healthcare).
Sometimes when querying a table that is loading, but it&#39;s deleted and then is reinserting a new row, you read that row twice. This is a known issue with isolation levels in SQL server - unless you have pessimistic levels set, which I can&#39;t due to users.
I therefore need to have some kind of hierarchical load process at scale (we have 100+ prod tables) to manage this problem. Airflow would work, but I don&#39;t know python.
I found some GUI alternatives I think, nifi was one?</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036221174780284938 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036221174780284938><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rakkit. data-user-id=209245848960368641>rakkit.</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 7:13 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1036221174780284938>10/30/2022 7:13 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>We ran into performance issues with merge due to the size of single tables and the number of rows processed incrementally.

I honestly just hoped there was an easier tool, I&#39;ve started making a &quot;queue&quot; for executing agent jobs in SQL server itself with dependency recorded in a table, where one job won&#39;t be put into a processing queue until it&#39;s requirements have completed.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036223927095144499 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036223927095144499><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/265514283901779970/257922a3b0fe6c0d1c40e94b7e10a655.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=corvuscrypto data-user-id=265514283901779970>Birdy (SE)</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 7:23 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1036223927095144499>10/30/2022 7:23 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>the key here is going to be capturing your dependency chain anyway so regardless of your approach you needed to start doing this (not just for yourself but for the entire org&#39;s usage)</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 7:31 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036224281228619806 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036224281228619806><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 7:25 AM">7:25 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>at large scale you can&#39;t sustain a &quot;everyone just load every x minutes/hours&quot; period and need to really force data producers to A) think about actually modelling the data for analytics usage before hitting the DW, and B) ensuring there is clean metadata all along the chain so that both systems and users can manage updates based on what changed in upstream sources</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036224516571021343 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036224516571021343><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 7:26 AM">7:26 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Airflow could help you short term for orchestration, but you&#39;d end up being bottlenecked by the DB at some point anyway</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 7:26 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036224923372376124 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036224923372376124><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 7:27 AM">7:27 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>also key here is making sure you understand the SLAs of datasets. Not all datasets will need such high speed loads (even in healthcare I guarantee not everything HAS to be reloaded with minute-scale speed), but people will default ofc to having it. What is critical, vs what can be delayed? Can you balance this somehow? Does it make sense to shunt higher-critical stuff to a separate DB? Is it feasible given budget/resources and how bad the problem is?</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 7:28 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036225152771444817 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036225152771444817><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 7:28 AM">7:28 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>the above also helps in the case you get ABSOLUTELY swamped and have to deprioritize work</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036226216333684806 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036226216333684806><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 7:33 AM">7:33 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote"><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-border"></div><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-content">The interdependencies for loading data marts is far too complex (and changes too often) for us to manage within containers/flows in SSIS since the management of that would be manual.
</div></div>this is common, btw, and the strategy is enforcing strict rules going forward on what metadata is required to build a dataset. You can ofc help get a base level of metadata in place around the datasets, but you have to be forcing everyone to abide by rules and use whoever you can to help you build out this culture of making sure dependencies are declared and known by producers</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036233315495198741 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036233315495198741><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rakkit. data-user-id=209245848960368641>rakkit.</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 8:01 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1036233315495198741>10/30/2022 8:01 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>That&#39;s really helpful, thanks. What do you mean by &quot;producers&quot;?</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036233402506031134 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036233402506031134><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/265514283901779970/257922a3b0fe6c0d1c40e94b7e10a655.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=corvuscrypto data-user-id=265514283901779970>Birdy (SE)</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 8:01 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1036233402506031134>10/30/2022 8:01 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>generators of upstream data</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036233612871356416 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036233612871356416><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 8:02 AM">8:02 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>you may not actually have a proper definition of this tbf, especially if you are transitioning from being a smaller user of data to larger and are mostly relying on production db snapshots</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036235110854443028 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036235110854443028><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 8:08 AM">8:08 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>a better way to put all of this is that you are getting large enough to have problems cascade to you due to volume. So, what information would help you manage all of this. You already built out some good strategies around dependencies, but what else can help you and your team more efficiently manage the data you need to process? Make that helpful data a requirement on other teams that want their data in your data warehouse and justify it on the basis that the company is at risk of degraded analytics, and inability to isolate critical workloads due to the lack of this data.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 8:12 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036256602417807360 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036256602417807360><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/105378403699408896/6ad9a21f4adaeee654f83a08a1327a68.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=rakkit.>rakkit.</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1036221174780284938')"> We ran into performance issues with merge due to the size of single tables and the number of rows processed incrementally.
We use SSIS to pull data from a few sources and dump replicas into SQL server.
The interdependencies for loading data marts is far too complex (and changes too often) for us to manage within containers/flows in SSIS since the management of that would be manual.
I honestly just hoped there was an easier tool, I&#39;ve started making a &quot;queue&quot; for executing agent jobs in SQL server itself with dependency recorded in a table, where one job won&#39;t be put into a processing queue until it&#39;s requirements have completed. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(231,76,60) title=emikachi data-user-id=105378403699408896>emily</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 9:33 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1036256602417807360>10/30/2022 9:33 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>fwiw, this is exactly what we did at bigger scales in SSIS. we encapsulated at the package level and had a table of package dependencies. during an execution, they were scheduled accordingly</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 9:34 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036256666099916870 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036256666099916870><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 9:34 AM">9:34 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>we did have to build that tool</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036261647876108349 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036261647876108349><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rakkit. data-user-id=209245848960368641>rakkit.</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 9:53 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1036261647876108349>10/30/2022 9:53 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Any tips <span class="chatlog__markdown-mention" title="emikachi">@emily</span> whilst I&#39;m in the infancy of building such a thing? What would you do differently if you started again?</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036275304068550736 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036275304068550736><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/105378403699408896/6ad9a21f4adaeee654f83a08a1327a68.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(231,76,60) title=emikachi data-user-id=105378403699408896>emily</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 10:48 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1036275304068550736>10/30/2022 10:48 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><span class="chatlog__markdown-mention" title="rakkit.">@rakkit.</span> it was a few of years ago now so my details are hazy, and I imagine you&#39;ll have most of this covered already, but:
<ul><li>There were 4 tables: Packages (executable packages), PackageDependencies (edges of Package-&gt;Package dependencies), ExecutionQueue (active work queues), ExecutionQueueHistory (work queue history for reporting)</li><li>You need to have checks gating updates to the dependency list to make sure it stays acyclic</li><li>We initially ran the packages through agent jobs (as in each package execution created and destroyed its own agent job). i wasn&#39;t involved at that point, but if I recall it was done partly for observability. it didn&#39;t work out that well and caused some pain in the msdb database. it should have been done directly through the SSISDB stored procedures e.g. <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">SSISDB.catalog.create_execution</code> </li><li>make sure the number of workers you are using is capped if your resources are capped. 30 parallel executions on 8 cores is not a good time</li><li>it&#39;s useful to include a loose &quot;priority&quot; on the datasets/packages, so you can force some things to be scheduled before others when you have a fixed number of workers. this can be derived from your SLAs if you have them. </li><li>also useful is a mechanism for retries and a backoff period (retry up to 5 times, wait 5 minutes between tries)</li><li>you also really, <em>really</em> need some better mechanisms of looking at what&#39;s currently running. We had a nice PowerBI dashboard, but even some views that look at the current executions goes a long way</li></ul></span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1036330837035200512 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1036330837035200512><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title="Deleted User" data-user-id=456226577798135808>Deleted User</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, October 30, 2022 2:28 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1036330837035200512>10/30/2022 2:28 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>anyone have any suggestions on building a data pipeline where the source is an external api and each team on an app will have their own API key to that external API? the pipeline needs to fetch the data daily</span></div></div></div></div></div>

So, I think I&#39;ll go with Data Analysis for the following reasons:-

1) Since DA is going to be a mix of both, it&#39;ll give me to exposure to find what I can tolerate better, and depending upon that I may got to DE or SDE in the future, hopefully  (or I&#39;ll just stick with DA if it works out well) 

2) I don&#39;t see as many job opportunities for DE, talking about junior positions, as I see for SDE and DA. 

3) Between SDE and DA, I think it&#39;s easier and faster for me to prepare for DA. They mainly ask aptitude, case studies, guesstimates in the shortlisting procedure for DA. While, in SDE, I&#39;d have to give a lot of time to practicing DSA to be able to solve the technical tests in almost all companies.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1038507137552351322 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1038507137552351322><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=armslegshandsfeet data-user-id=466248882335252500>armslegshandsfeet</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, November 5, 2022 2:36 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1038507137552351322>11/5/2022 2:36 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>My coworker discovered that BQ doesn&#39;t do a great job with aggregations and joins in the same CTE / subquery. So if you do something like:
<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline nohighlight">select id
from customer
inner join order
on customer_id.id = order.customer_id
group by 1</code>
that will physically join the tables before aggregating. But if you do

<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline nohighlight">with customer as (
select id
from customer
group by 1
),
select customer.id
from customer
inner join order
on customer.id = order.customer_id</code>
it&#39;ll properly aggregate before the join. On tables with 2m x 1.5b rows, this can be a big deal.</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=open_mouth><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=😮 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f62e.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>2</span></div></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1038507300207468564 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1038507300207468564><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, November 5, 2022 2:37 PM">2:37 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>We reduced slot time usage by 90% on that CTE.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
